Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Identifying a Classical Logic Text
Editorial title page identifies the work, author, and modern commentator.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract the key bibliographic details (author, work, editor, publisher) from the title page of a classical Islamic work.

Core Idea
The title page is the entry key to a work's scholarly pedigree.

Before diving into the logical content of al-Sullam al-Murawnaq, we must first understand what this book is and who produced it. A title page tells us not just the name, but also the author, editor, and scholarly lineage. This lesson will train you to read such front matter critically, as it is the first step in evaluating any text in the Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work's full title
Look at the Arabic title: السلم المرونق في علم المنطق. This tells you the subject (logic) and that it is a didactic poem (sullam means ladder, but here it is a poetic mnemonic).
2
Identify the original author
The next line mentions ناظمها (its versifier) followed by the author: عبد الرحمن الأخضري. Note his death date (953 AH) and his regional/legal affiliation (الجزائري المالكي). This helps place him in Islamic intellectual history.
3
Identify the modern editor and publisher
The editor is أبو بكر بلقاسم ضيف الجزائري, and the publisher is دار ابن حزم. The phrase تحقيق وتقديم وتعليق indicates critical edition, introduction, and commentary. This tells you the edition is academically supervised.
4
Understand the series context
The top line سلسلة تحقيق التراث الجزائري shows this is part of a series aimed at reviving Algerian heritage. This gives you the broader intellectual project behind the edition.
Knowing the series helps assess the editorial priorities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سلسلة تحقيق التراث الجزائري
السلم المرونق في علم المنطق
شرح ناظمها العلامة عبد الرحمن الأخضري الجزائري المالكي
المتوفي سنة ٩٥٣ هـ
تحقيق وتقديم وتعليق أبو بكر بلقاسم ضيف الجزائري
دار ابن حزم
Series of Investigating Algerian Heritage
The Ornamented Ladder in the Science of Logic
Commentary on its versifier, the scholar Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari al-Jaza'iri al-Maliki
Who died in the year 953 AH
Investigation, introduction, and commentary by Abu Bakr Belqasim Daif al-Jaza'iri
Dar Ibn Hazm
Source pages p. 1

Commentary
This passage presents the bibliographic front matter of the edition. It identifies the series as the Series of Investigating Algerian Heritage, the work as al-Sullam al-Murawnaq fi 'Ilm al-Mantiq, the original versifier as Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari al-Jaza'iri al-Maliki who died in 953 AH, and the editor as Abu Bakr Belqasim Daif al-Jaza'iri. The publisher Dar Ibn Hazm is also named.

Key Terms

تحقيق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who is the original author of al-Sullam al-Murawnaq?
A) Abu Bakr Belqasim Daif
B) Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari
C) Ibn Hazm
D) Al-Maliki

Key Takeaway
A title page is not mere decoration; it is the first tool for critically situating any Islamic text in its scholarly tradition.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find a scanned copy of a classical Islamic text (e.g., Mukhtasar al-Quduri or al-Ajurrumiyya). Write down the author, editor (if any), publisher, and publication date from the title page. Then explain why each piece of information matters for studying that text.
?
Compare the title page of this edition of al-Sullam al-Murawnaq with another edition. Are there differences in the editor, publisher, or series? How might those affect the reliability of the text?

Introduction and Front Matter

Anatomy of a Critical Edition Introduction
Editor outlines introduction topics for critical edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the standard components of a modern critical edition of a classical Islamic logic text and explain the purpose of each component.

Core Idea
A critical edition's introduction bridges the classical author's world and the modern reader, establishing textual authority and scholarly context.

Before diving into al-Akhdari's versified logic poem, we must understand the editorial framework surrounding it. This lesson parses the editor's outline to reveal how a modern tahqiq edition situates a classical text: through biography, source criticism, manuscript analysis, methodology, and a definitional overview of the science itself. Mastering this structure will help you navigate any critical edition of an Islamic scholarly work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and text
Locate the name 'Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari' and the title 'al-Sullam al-Murawnaq' in the outline. Recognize that the edition is centered on his versified logic primer and his own commentary.
The title al-Sullam al-Murawnaq means 'The Embellished Ladder'.
2
List the biographical topics covered
Scan the outline for personal details: birth, lineage, environment, education, teachers, scholarly brilliance, works, scientific stature, and death. Each serves to establish al-Akhdari's authority and intellectual background.
Biographical research helps verify attributions and contextualize the text.
3
Distinguish classical content from editorial apparatus
Separate the items that belong to the classical tradition (definition of logic, subject matter, benefit, etc.) from modern editorial concerns (manuscripts, methodology, facsimiles). The former repeats what medieval mutakallimun typically discussed; the latter is the editor's contribution.
Understanding this boundary prevents confusing the editor's voice with the author's.
4
Recognize the purpose of each section
Reflect on why each element appears: biography grounds the author; sources show his influences; manuscripts establish textual reliability; methodology ensures transparency; definition of logic reminds the reader of the science's scope before studying the poem.
This outline is a roadmap for the entire introduction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة المحقق
عبدالرحمن الأخضري.
مولده، نسبه البيئة والمنشأ تعلمه وشيوخه، نبوغه في العلم، مؤلفاته، البعد العلمي للأخضري، وفاته.
المصادر التي اعتمد عليها الأخضري في شرح سلمه.
النسخ المعتمدة من كتاب السلم المرونق في علم المنطق.
منهجي في الإعداد والتحقيق.
تعريف علم المنطق، موضوعه، فائدته ثمرته نسبته واضعه
اسمه، استمداده مسائله.
الصفحة الأولى والأخيرة من المخطوطة (أ).
الصفحة الأولى والاخيرة من المخطوطة (ب).
Editor's Introduction
Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari.
His birth, his lineage, his environment and upbringing, his education and his shaykhs, his brilliance in knowledge, his works, the scientific stature of al-Akhdari, and his death.
The sources upon which al-Akhdari relied in his commentary on his Sullam.
The relied-upon manuscripts of the book al-Sullam al-Murawnaq in the science of logic.
My methodology in preparation and verification.
The definition of the science of logic, its subject matter, its benefit, its fruit, its relation, its founder,
its name, its derivation, its issues.
The first and last page of manuscript (A).
The first and last page of manuscript (B).
Source pages p. 2

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents outlining the editor's introduction to the critical edition. The editor announces that he will begin with a biographical study of Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari, covering his birth, lineage, environment, education, teachers, scholarly brilliance, written works, scientific stature, and death. He then lists the sources al-Akhdari used in composing his commentary on al-Sullam, the manuscripts relied upon for establishing this edition, and the editorial methodology he himself employed. Finally, he notes that the introduction will address the definition of logic, its subject matter, benefit, fruit, relation to other sciences, founder, name, etymology, and the issues it treats, followed by a codicological description of the two manuscript witnesses. This structure follows the conventional apparatus of a modern tahqiq edition, framing the classical text within contemporary academic standards.

السلم المرونق
تحقيق

Checkpoint
According to the editor's outline, which of the following topics is NOT explicitly listed as part of the introduction?
A) The biography of Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari
B) The definition of logic and its subject matter
C) The manuscripts relied upon for the edition
D) A complete commentary on al-Abhari's Isaghuji

Key Takeaway
A critical edition's introduction systematically establishes the author's authority, the text's sources and manuscript basis, the editor's methodology, and the science's foundational definitions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
List the components you would expect to find in a critical edition of a major hadith collection like Sahih al-Bukhari, based on the model outlined here.
?
Compare the editor's outline with the table of contents of a classical logic text such as al-Abhari's *Isaghuji*: what topics overlap, and what does the modern editor add?

The Role of Ikhtisar in Logic Education
Editor prefaces the edition by praising heritage and introducing al-Akhdari's abbreviated Sharh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how al-Akhdari's method of ikhtisar made logic accessible to students and identify its sources from the classical tradition.

Core Idea
Abbreviation (ikhtisar) is a pedagogical tradition that distills complex knowledge into teachable form.

In this editor's preface, we see how al-Akhdari's Sharh al-Sullam fits into a long tradition of pedagogical abbreviation. The editor highlights that al-Akhdari took the dense, multi-volume works of major logicians like al-Shirazi, al-Taftazani, al-Iji, and al-Abhari and simplified them into a concise verse commentary. Understanding this process helps us appreciate how Islamic logic was taught and transmitted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the editor's preface
Read the opening and note what the editor wants to convey about the work's significance. Specifically, look for phrases like 'important risala' and 'for knowing the science of logic'.
The editor also praises the heritage and those who work on it.
2
List the major logic texts al-Akhdari condensed
From the passage, find the names of scholars and works that al-Akhdari drew upon: al-Shirazi, al-Taftazani, al-Iji, and al-Abhari's Isaghuji.
These are among the core references in the Eastern logical tradition.
3
Examine the term ikhtisar
Consider how the editor describes al-Akhdari's method: 'abbreviation' (ikhtisar) and 'simplified with utmost simplicity' (fi ghayat al-basata). What does 'bast' contribute?
Bast means expansion for clarity, here applied to the abbreviation process.
4
Assess the pedagogical value
Reflect on why an abbreviation would be important for students. The editor says it is 'important for knowing the science of logic and understanding it' – how does brevity aid learning?
Abbreviation allowed students to memorize and grasp essentials before moving to detailed works.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
وبه نستعين
مقدمة المحقق
الحمد لله والصلاة والسلام على رسول الله وعلى آله وصحبه ومن والاه، أما بعد:
[من؟]
إن التراث العربي الإسلامي الجزائري حافل وكبير وكثير وهو متفرق بين زوايا ومكتبات الجزائر ويجدر بي أن أنوه بالأساتذة والباحثين الذين يسهرون على إخراج التراث العربي الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد من تحقيق وتعليق وترتيب، وإعداد، وها نحن أخرجنا سلسلتنا في تحقيق كتب المنطق رسالة العلامة اللوذعي والإمام الألمعي حجة عصره وفريد دهره السيد الشيخ عبدالرحمن الأخضري الجزائري الموسومة بشرح متن السلم المرونق في علم المنطق وهي رسالة مهمة لمعرفة علم المنطق وفهمه وذلك للاختصار الذي أخرجه العلامة عبد الرحمن الأخضري من مطولات كتب المنطق ككتب القطب فخر الدين الشيرازي وسعد الدين التفتازاني، وعضد الدين الإيجي والأبهري على إيساغوجي، حيث بسطه في غاية البساطة، ونحن قمنا بترتيبه وتحقيقه والتعليق عليه وقد اعتمدنا في تحقيقنا على
(۱) ونظم السلم هو من كتاب إيساغوجي للأبهري.
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful.
And by Him we seek help.
Editor's Introduction
All praise is due to Allah and prayer and peace be upon the Messenger of Allah and upon his family and his companions and whoever allies with him. As for what follows:
[from?]
Indeed the Algerian Arab-Islamic heritage is abundant and great and plentiful, and it is dispersed among the corners and libraries of Algeria, and it behooves me that I note the professors and researchers who stay up late to bring out the Arab-Islamic heritage in its new garb of verification, commentary, arrangement, and preparation. And here we have brought out our series in verifying the books of logic: the risala of the scholar al-Lawdahi and the Imam, the brilliant one, the proof of his time and the unique one of his age, al-Sayyid al-Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari al-Jazairi, entitled Sharh Matn al-Sullam al-Murawnaq in the science of logic. And it is an important risala for knowing the science of logic and understanding it, and that is due to the abbreviation that the scholar Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari produced from the lengthy books of logic such as the books of Qutb al-Din al-Shirazi and Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani and 'Adud al-Din al-Iji and al-Abhari on the Isaghuji, for he simplified it with utmost simplicity. And we have arranged it, verified it, and commented upon it, and we have relied in our verification upon
(1) And the versification of al-Sullam is from the book Isaghuji of al-Abhari.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage opens the editor's preface to the critical edition. The author begins with the customary basmala, hamdala, and salawat, then turns to praise the Algerian Arab-Islamic heritage and acknowledge the scholars working to edit and publish it. He introduces this volume as part of a series dedicated to editing logic books, specifically presenting the commentary of Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari on al-Sullam al-Murawnaq. He emphasizes the importance of this particular work by noting that al-Akhdari distilled the lengthy treatments found in the major logic texts—such as those by al-Shirazi, al-Taftazani, al-Iji, and al-Abhari's Isaghuji—into an extremely simplified and accessible form. The editor then states that his own contribution has been to arrange, verify, and comment upon this text, and he begins to describe his editorial methodology before the excerpt ends. The footnote clarifies that the versified poem al-Sullam belongs to the tradition of al-Abhari's Isaghuji.

الاختصار
إيساغوجي
بسط

C) Because it introduces new logical proofs unknown to earlier scholars

Key Takeaway
Al-Akhdari's Sharh al-Sullam exemplifies the Islamic pedagogical method of ikhtisar, making advanced logic accessible through concise abbreviation and simplification.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Place of al-Akhdari's Sullam in the Logical Tradition
Editor introduces his critical edition and acknowledges bibliographic sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the chains of textual transmission in Islamic logic and explain how al-Akhdari's Sullam summarizes earlier authoritative works.

Core Idea
Al-Akhdari's Sullam is a distillation of the classical logical tradition, not an innovation.

This preface introduces us to the editorial project and, more importantly, reveals how al-Akhdari's work fits into the broader logical tradition. Understanding this context helps us appreciate why the Sullam became a standard teaching text in North African madrasas. The editor explicitly names the major authorities whose lengthy discussions al-Akhdari condensed, showing that the Sullam is a pedagogical summary rather than an independent treatise.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the genre: editorial preface
Note the doxological opening (basmala, hamdala, salawat), the naming of the work and its author, and the description of editorial labor (tahqiq, ta'liq, tartib). This frames the text as a critical edition intended to serve scholars.
Editorial prefaces often contain valuable information about the textual tradition and the work's place in the curriculum.
2
Identify the sources al-Akhdari drew upon
The editor lists the books of al-Shirazi, al-Taftazani, al-Iji, and al-Abhari (on Isaghuji) as the lengthy sources from which al-Akhdari extracted his concise text. Recognizing these names helps situate the Sullam within the post-classical logical tradition.
Each of these authors wrote extensive commentaries; al-Akhdari's ikhtisar made logic accessible to beginners.
3
Assess the significance of brevity (ikhtisar)
The editor praises al-Akhdari for producing a text of 'utmost simplicity' from complex material. In the madrasa tradition, ikhtisar is a valued pedagogical genre: a short text that encapsulates essential knowledge, often memorized and then studied with a commentary.
The Sullam is itself a matn; al-Akhdari's own sharh (commentary) on his matn is what the present edition provides.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
وبه نستعين
مقدمة المحقق
الحمد لله والصلاة والسلام على رسول الله وعلى آله وصحبه ومن والاه، أما بعد:
إن التراث العربي الإسلامي الجزائري حافل وكبير وكثير وهو متفرق بين زوايا ومكتبات الجزائر ويجدر بي أن أنوه بالأساتذة والباحثين الذين يسهرون على إخراج التراث العربي الإسلامي في ثوبه الجديد من تحقيق وتعليق وترتيب ،وإعداد، وها نحن أخرجنا سلسلتنا في تحقيق كتب المنطق رسالة العلامة اللوذعي[؟] والإمام الألمعي حجة عصره وفريد دهره السيد الشيخ عبدالرحمن الأخضري الجزائري الموسومة بشرح متن السلم المرونق في علم المنطق وهي رسالة مهمة لمعرفة علم المنطق وفهمه وذلك للاختصار الذي أخرجه العلامة عبد الرحمن الأخضري من مطولات كتب المنطق ككتب القطب فخر الدين الشيرازي وسعد الدين التفتازاني، وعضد الدين الإيجي والأبهري على إيساغوجي ، حيث بسطه في غاية البساطة، ونحن قمنا بترتيبه وتحقيقه والتعليق عليه وقد اعتمدنا في تحقيقنا على البحاثة العلامة التراث وباعثه من جديد الشيخ بشير ضيف بن أبي بكر محي الجزائري في كتبه المخطوطة :
العقود والجواهر في الكشف عن مخطوطات علماء الجزائر ٤ أجزاء مخطوط. العقود اللؤلؤية في الكشف عن المطبوعات العربية الجزائرية ٤ أجزاء مخطوط. أوائل المطبوعات العربية في الجزائر بالصور مخطوط.
عنوان الأريب فيما ألف كتاباً بوادي ميزاب من عالم أو أديب مخطوط. ولا أعلم أحداً سبق الشيخ في جمع وإحصاء تراث العلامة عبدالرحمن الأخضري فله مني الشكر الأوفى والجزاء حتى يرضى.
(۱) ونظم السلم هو من كتاب إيساغوجي للأبهري.
In the name of Allah, the Merciful, the Compassionate
And by Him we seek help
Preface of the Investigator
All praise is due to Allah and prayer and peace be upon the Messenger of Allah and upon his family and his companions and whoever allies with him. As for what follows:
Indeed the Algerian Arab Islamic heritage is ample and great and abundant, and it is dispersed among the corners and libraries of Algeria, and it behooves me to note the professors and researchers who stay up at night to bring out the Arab Islamic heritage in its new garb of investigation, commentary, arrangement, and preparation. And here we have brought out our series in investigating the books of logic, the treatise of the learned luminary[?] and the brilliant imam, the proof of his time and the unique one of his age, the master shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari the Algerian, entitled Sharh Matn al-Sullam al-Murawnaq fi 'Ilm al-Mantiq, and it is an important treatise for knowing the science of logic and understanding it, and that is due to the brevity that the luminary Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari produced from the lengthy books of logic such as the books of the pole Fakhr al-Din al-Shirazi and Sa'd al-Din al-Taftazani, and 'Adud al-Din al-Iji and al-Abhari on the Isaghuji, for he elaborated it with utmost simplicity. And we have undertaken its arrangement, investigation, and commentary upon it, and we have relied in our investigation upon the researcher luminary [of] heritage and its reviver Shaykh Bashir Dayf ibn Abi Bakr Muhyi al-Jaza'iri in his handwritten books:
al-'Uqud wa al-Jawahir fi al-Kashf 'an Makhṭutat 'Ulama' al-Jaza'ir, 4 volumes, manuscript. al-'Uqud al-Lu'lu'iyya fi al-Kashf 'an al-Matbu'at al-'Arabiyya al-Jaza'iriyya, 4 volumes, manuscript. Awai'l al-Matbu'at al-'Arabiyya fi al-Jaza'ir bi-al-Suwar, manuscript. 'Unwan al-Arib fi-ma Ullifa Kitaban bi-Wadi Mizab min 'Alim aw Adib, manuscript. And I do not know anyone who preceded the Shaykh in collecting and enumerating the heritage of the luminary Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari, so to him belongs from me the fullest thanks and reward until he is pleased.
(1) And the versification of al-Sullam is from the book Isaghuji of al-Abhari.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is a modern editorial preface in which the investigator introduces his critical edition of al-Akhdari's commentary on the Sullam. The editor begins with the standard doxological opening, then turns to the state of Algerian Islamic heritage, noting its abundance and its dispersal across libraries. He acknowledges the broader scholarly effort to recover and publish this heritage through critical editing, commentary, arrangement, and preparation. He then situates his own contribution within this effort, presenting a series dedicated to logic texts. The specific work under consideration is al-Akhdari's Sharh Matn al-Sullam al-Murawnaq, praised for its brevity and clarity. The editor emphasizes that al-Akhdari distilled the lengthy discussions found in major logic works—such as those by Shirazi, Taftazani, Iji, and Abhari's Isaghuji—into an accessible format. He describes the editorial labor undertaken: arrangement, investigation, and commentary. Finally, he acknowledges his dependence on the bibliographic researches of Shaykh Bashir Dayf, listing the latter's manuscript works on Algerian scholarly production, and expresses gratitude for Dayf's pioneering collection of al-Akhdari's heritage. The footnote adds a note on the relationship between the Sullam and Abhari's Isaghuji.

Key Terms
تحقيق
تعليق
السلم المرونق
إيساغوجي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) He extracted brevity from lengthy books of logic by earlier authorities

D) He translated Greek logic into Arabic

Key Takeaway
Al-Akhdari's Sullam is a pedagogical summary of the classical logical tradition, not an independent innovation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the editor's preface, list the four authoritative logicians whose works al-Akhdari summarized. Then, for each, find one logical doctrine they are known for (e.g., Taftazani on definitions, Abhari on the Isagoge).
?
Compare the opening lines of al-Akhdari's Sullam (if available) with the opening of al-Abhari's Isaghuji. What structural similarities or differences do you observe in how they introduce the subject of logic?

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Assessing a Text's Authority Through Its Preface
Editor introduces the logic series and al-Akhdari's scholarly rank.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify markers of a classical text's authoritativeness in an editor's preface: global curriculum adoption, multigenerational commentary tradition, and the author's scholarly rank.

Core Idea
A text's adoption as a matn muqarrar and its layered commentaries signal its logical authority.

When you pick up a critical edition of a classical Islamic logic text, the editor's preface is not mere ceremony. It tells you why this text matters, who wrote it, and how it was received. This lesson trains you to read that preface for the evidence it offers about the text's scholarly weight and pedigree.

Guided Path
1
Identify the editorial project
The editor names a series of logic editions (Sharh al-Sullam, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Mantiq, Lub al-Lubab). What does this series include? Why does he list them?
The series establishes the contemporary scholarly environment and the lineage of the edition.
2
Extract the evidence of the text's diffusion
The editor says al-Akhdari's commentary was adopted as a matn muqarrar at al-Azhar and al-Zaytunah and translated into French. What does that tell you about its reach?
A matn muqarrar is a prescribed curricular text, indicating institutional endorsement.
3
Assess the commentary tradition
The editor notes the text generated shuruh, ta'liq, and istidrak. What do these layers imply about the text's profundity and the scholarly attention it received?
Each layer represents a different level of scholarly engagement: full commentaries, glosses, and corrections.
4
Evaluate the author's rank
The editor praises al-Akhdari's mastery of transmitted and rational sciences at a young age. How does this biographical note reinforce the text's authority?
A young author's deep knowledge suggests natural intellectual preeminence.

Surely to Allah we belong and to Him we shall return. And finally I supplicate Allah, Mighty and Majestic, that He make my deed sincere for His Noble Face. And I thank again my brother, the learned researcher Sheikh Bashir Daif for opening his library to us, which is abundant with the treasures of the Islamic Ummah, when this edition came to light. And may Allah bless our master Muhammad and his family and companions and grant them peace. Abu Bakr Belqasim Daif al-Jazairi. 15 Ramadan 1425 AH - 30 October 2004 CE.
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is a prefatory dedication in which the editor situates the volume within a larger editorial project devoted to logic texts. He opens by praising Sheikh Bashir Daif as a reviver of heritage and lists his bibliographic manuscripts on Algerian scholars and publications. He notes that no one preceded Sheikh Bashir in collecting and enumerating the legacy of Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari, and he offers him sincere thanks. He then names the logic series to which this edition belongs: Sharh al-Sullam by Ibrahim Sa'id Qudura al-Jazairi, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Mantiq by al-Sanusi, Lub al-Lubab fi Radd al-Fikr ila al-Sawab by Abd al-Karim al-Maghili, and the present book, al-Akhdari's commentary on his own Sullam. The editor observes that this text has generated abundant commentaries, glosses, and corrections, and that it is a set text at major Islamic institutes such as al-Azhar al-Sharif and the Zaytunah Mosque, and that it was translated into French. He takes this as proof of the author's high standing and deep penetration into the transmitted and rational sciences at an age before he had even reached full maturity. The editor then muses that had al-Akhdari been granted a longer life, he would have filled the world with knowledge, but fate is fixed by divine decree, and when a man's term arrives it neither hastens nor delays. He concludes with a prayer for sincerity, a second thanks to Sheikh Bashir for opening his library, and the salutation upon the Prophet.

The Textual Tradition of al-Sullam al-Murawnaq
Author lists al-Sullam's origin, manuscripts, and commentators

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to trace the manuscript and commentary tradition of al-Sullam al-Murawnaq and explain its relationship to al-Abhari's Sharh Isaghuji.

Core Idea
Al-Sullam is a 94-verse poem that condenses the entire Isagoge commentary tradition into a memorizable ladder.

This lesson introduces you to the physical map of the Sullam tradition. You will learn where the manuscripts are, who commented on the poem, and why this matters for understanding how logic was taught in North African madrasas. The passage provides a bibliographic snapshot that connects al-Akhdari's work to the wider Islamic textual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of al-Sullam
Find the statement that al-Sullam was versified from Sharh Isaghuji by al-Abhari. Note that it is not an original composition but a pedagogical condensation.
This shows how didactic poems rely on earlier prose commentaries.
2
Locate the manuscript evidence
List the libraries mentioned: Berlin, Gotha, British Museum. Also note the printed editions in Bulaq (1241 AH) and Fes (1317 AH) and the French translation by Luciani.
These details demonstrate the geographic spread and scholarly interest in the text.
3
Recognize the commentary tradition
Identify the two commentators named: Sa'id ibn Ibrahim Qadura (d. 1066 AH) and Ali ibn Ahmad al-Adawi (d. 1189 AH). Note where their commentaries exist in manuscript and print.
Each commentator adds a layer of interpretation, making the Sullam a living text.
4
Assess the significance of the footnote
Read the footnote (1) at the end of the passage. It provides additional bibliographic sources for verifying the manuscript data.
This shows the scholarly practice of citing sources for textual verification.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Al-Akhdari's Stature and the Sullam: A Didactic Bridge to Logic
Author assesses al-Akhdari's genius and describes his versified logic primer al-Sullam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of al-Sullam as a versified logic primer and situate it within the madrasa tradition.

Core Idea
Al-Sullam makes logic memorisable through verse without sacrificing precision.

This lesson introduces Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari, the 10th-century scholar whose rajaz poem al-Sullam al-Murawnaq became a staple of North African logic education. We examine how al-Akhdari's encyclopedic mastery of the Islamic sciences shaped his approach to logic, and how his versification of al-Abhari's Sharh Isaghuji transformed a prose logic text into a memorisable teaching tool.

Guided Path
1
Recognize al-Akhdari's scholarly scope
Note the range of sciences al-Akhdari mastered: jurisprudence (fiqh), monotheism (tawhid), Sufism (tasawwuf), inheritance law (faraid), rhetoric (balagha), grammar (nahw), astronomy (falak), and others. This breadth explains why his logic primer is pedagogically effective.
His comprehensive learning ensured that his logic text integrates insights from diverse Islamic fields.
2
Identify the Sullam's source text
The Sullam is a versification of Imam al-Abhari's Sharh Isaghuji, not an independent work. This lineage places it within the Isaghuji commentary tradition.
Understanding this lineage helps you trace the logical concepts back to their systematic exposition in al-Abhari.
3
Understand the didactic function of rajaz
Rajaz meter makes the poem easy to memorize while preserving technical content. This is a common feature of Islamic didactic poems (manzumat).
Memorization of the poem ensures that the logical framework is deeply embedded in the student's mind.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عالية وموهبة فذة زرعت فيه النبوغ العلمي المبكر، الأمر الذي جعل ذهنه الجبار يهضم غالب علوم عصره من فقه وتوحيد وتصوف وفرائض وبلاغة ونحو وفلك وغيرها.
لهذا نستطيع القول أن الشيخ عبدالرحمن الأخضري كان موسوعة علمية نادرة الوجود في تاريخنا الثقافي خاصة العهد العثماني الذي عاش الأخضري في بدايته.

High intelligence and a unique talent planted in him early scientific genius, the matter which made his mighty mind digest most of the sciences of his age from jurisprudence, monotheism, Sufism, inheritance law, rhetoric, grammar, astronomy, and other than them.
For this we are able to say that Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari was a rare encyclopedic scientific figure in our cultural history, especially the Ottoman era which al-Akhdari lived at its beginning.

Commentary
This passage introduces the author of the Sullam and his intellectual environment. It opens by describing Shaykh Abd al-Rahman al-Akhdari's extraordinary natural endowment and early scientific genius, noting that his powerful intellect mastered the vast majority of his era's sciences: jurisprudence (fiqh), monotheism (tawhid), Sufism (tasawwuf), inheritance law (faraid), rhetoric (balagha), grammar (nahw), astronomy (falak), and others. From this the author concludes that al-Akhdari was a rare encyclopedic figure in Islamic cultural history, particularly during the early Ottoman period in which he lived. The passage then turns to his works, focusing on al-Sullam al-Murawnaq fi Ilm al-Mantiq. It identifies this work as a poem of ninety-four rajaz verses, which al-Akhdari versified from the book Sharh Isaghuji of Imam al-Abhari. It further records the poem's manuscript presence in major libraries—Berlin, Gotha, and the British Museum—and its print history in Bulaq in 1241 AH and in Fez in 1317 AH, as well as its translation into French by Luciani. The footnote supplies modern bibliographic references supporting these details.

Mapping the Commentators of al-Sullam
Author lists commentators with dates and locations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main commentators of al-Sullam and trace the geographical and institutional distribution of their commentaries.

Core Idea
The Sullam commentary tradition spans centuries and continents, preserved in manuscripts and prints across libraries worldwide.

Al-Akhdari's Sullam attracted numerous commentaries. Knowing who wrote them, when, and where their works are found helps you understand the transmission and reception of this key logic text. This bibliographic list from the source grounds you in the commentary tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first commentator and his details
Locate the earliest author (by death date) in the list. Note his name, death year, and where his commentary is preserved (manuscript and print).
Sa'id ibn Ibrahim Qadura (d. 1066 AH) is first; his commentary is in the British Museum and Algeria's National Library, printed in Bulaq.
2
Compare print vs. manuscript distribution
For each commentator, check whether the passage mentions a printed edition or only manuscripts. Some have both, some only manuscripts.
e.g., al-Bajuri has both manuscript (Alexandria) and print (Cairo, Bulaq with gloss). Others like al-Adawi have only manuscript locations listed.
3
Map the geographical spread
Note the cities and libraries mentioned: Cairo, Alexandria, Berlin, Paris, Calcutta, etc. This shows the wide reach of the Sullam tradition.
The tradition extends from North Africa to Europe and Asia.
4
Identify the latest commentator and any distinctive features
Find the most recent author (Muhammad Atfish). Note his death in CE and his epithet 'Qutb al-A'imma'.
He died in 1914 CE, showing the tradition continued into the modern period.

شراح السلم
- سعيد بن إبراهيم قدورة المتوفي سنة ١٠٦٦هـ يوجد هذا الشرح في المتحف البريطاني ونسخة بالجزائر في المكتبة الوطنية وقد طبع هذا الشرح في بولاق بالقاهرة سنة ١٢٨٥هـ.
- علي بن أحمد العدوي المتوفي سنة ١١٨٩ يوجد هذا الشرح بالقاهرة والجزائر والرباط.
- إبراهيم الباجوري المتوفي سنة ١٢٧٧هـ، يوجد مخطوطاً في الإسكندرية وقد طبع في القاهرة سنة ١٢٨٢هـ مع حاشية الأنبابي ط بولاق سنة ١٢٩٧هـ.
- علي الديباجة إسماعيل المتوفي سنة ١١٥٠هـ، يوجد هذا الشرح في برلين والإسكندرية.
- أحمد بن محمد بن يعقوب الولالي المتوفي سنة ١١٢٨هـ، يوجد هذا الشرح في المتحف البريطاني، الجزائر، الرباط.
- عبدالوهاب بن قنديل الملوي المتوفي سنة ١١٦٠هـ، يوجد هذا الشرح في برلين والإسكندرية.
- أحمد بن عبدالفتاح بن يوسف الملوي المتوفي سنة ١١٨١هـ، يوجد هذا الشرح في برلين وجوتا وميونيخ وهاوبت، وباريس وكلكتا والإسكندرية.
- محمد الصالح محمد بن سليمان المشدالي.
- القاضي مبارك المتوفي سنة ١١٦٢هـ.
- أبي إسحاق إبراهيم بن محمد التادلي الإباضي المتوفي سنة ١٣٠٧هـ.
- محمد بن يوسف بن عيسى أطفيش الشهير بقطب الأئمة المتوفي سنة ١٩١٤م.
Commentators on al-Sullam:
- Sa'id ibn Ibrahim Qadura, who died in the year 1066 AH; this commentary exists in the British Museum and a copy in Algeria in the National Library, and this commentary was printed in Bulaq in Cairo in the year 1285 AH.
- Ali ibn Ahmad al-Adawi, who died in the year 1189 AH; this commentary exists in Cairo, Algeria, and Rabat.
- Ibrahim al-Bajuri, who died in the year 1277 AH; it exists in manuscript in Alexandria and was printed in Cairo in the year 1282 AH with the gloss of al-Anbabi, printed [t] Bulaq in the year 1297 AH.
- Ali al-Dibaja Isma'il, who died in the year 1150 AH; this commentary exists in Berlin and Alexandria.
- Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ya'qub al-Walali, who died in the year 1128 AH; this commentary exists in the British Museum, Algeria, Rabat.
- Abd al-Wahhab ibn Qandil al-Malawi, who died in the year 1160 AH; this commentary exists in Berlin and Alexandria.
- Ahmad ibn Abd al-Fattah ibn Yusuf al-Malawi, who died in the year 1181 AH; this commentary exists in Berlin, Gotha, Munich, Haupt, Paris, Calcutta, and Alexandria.
- Muhammad al-Salih Muhammad ibn Sulayman al-Mashdali.
- Al-Qadi Mubarak, who died in the year 1162 AH.
- Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Tadili al-Ibadi, who died in the year 1307 AH.
- Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Isa Atfish, known as Qutb al-A'imma, who died in the year 1914 CE.
Source pages p. 8

Commentary
This passage enumerates the principal commentators (shuruh) on al-Akhdari's Sullam. It begins with Sa'id ibn Ibrahim Qadura (d. 1066 AH), noting that his commentary is preserved in the British Museum and in a copy in Algeria's National Library, and that it was printed in Bulaq, Cairo, in 1285 AH. Next is Ali ibn Ahmad al-Adawi (d. 1189 AH), whose commentary is found in Cairo, Algeria, and Rabat. The list continues with Ibrahim al-Bajuri (d. 1277 AH), whose commentary exists in manuscript in Alexandria and was printed in Cairo in 1282 AH together with the gloss of al-Anbabi, and again in Bulaq in 1297 AH. Then Ali al-Dibaja Isma'il (d. 1150 AH), with manuscripts in Berlin and Alexandria. Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ya'qub al-Walali (d. 1128 AH) has commentaries in the British Museum, Algeria, and Rabat. Abd al-Wahhab ibn Qandil al-Malawi (d. 1160 AH) is represented in Berlin and Alexandria. Ahmad ibn Abd al-Fattah ibn Yusuf al-Malawi (d. 1181 AH) has manuscripts spread across Berlin, Gotha, Munich, Haupt, Paris, Calcutta, and Alexandria. The list also includes Muhammad al-Salih ibn Sulayman al-Mashdali, al-Qadi Mubarak (d. 1162 AH), Abu Ishaq Ibrahim ibn Muhammad al-Tadili al-Ibadi (d. 1307 AH), and finally Muhammad ibn Yusuf ibn Isa Atfish, known as Qutb al-A'imma (d. 1914 CE). The passage thereby maps the wide geographical and institutional diffusion of the Sullam commentary tradition.

Mapping the Glossators on al-Sullam
Author lists the glossators on al-Sullam and their print history.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the role of ḥawāshī in the logic curriculum and locate the works listed in this passage.

Core Idea
Glosses (ḥawāshī) on al-Sullam reveal a vibrant tradition of close textual commentary.

After the major commentaries (shurūḥ) on al-Sullam, later scholars added glosses (ḥawāshī) that often expanded on specific points or corrected earlier interpretations. This passage names two such glossators and gives their death dates and where their works can be found. Learning to read these bibliographic entries is essential for tracing the transmission of logical texts in the Islamic West.

Guided Path
1
Identify the genre: ḥāshiya vs. sharḥ
Note that the passage explicitly uses the term ḥawāshī (glosses), not shurūḥ (commentaries). A ḥāshiya is usually a marginal note, often shorter and more focused than a full commentary. This distinction matters for understanding the depth and scope of the work.
2
Extract the bibliographic data
Read each entry carefully: name of the glossator, death date (in AH), and location (print or manuscript). For al-Ṣabbān, we have a print date and place; for al-ʿAdawī, we have manuscript locations. This tells us how the text circulated.
3
Consult the footnote reference
The footnote (1) cites two Algerian bibliographic sources: ʿUqūd al-Jawāhir and al-ʿUqūd al-Luʾluʾiyya. These are standard references for works of logic. Knowing these sources helps verify the list.
4
Reflect on the curriculum significance
The existence of multiple glosses shows that al-Sullam was a core text studied and taught over centuries. Each glossator added his own insights, allowing us to see how the discipline evolved.

الحواشي على السلم (١)
محمد بن علي الصبان المتوفي سنة ١٢٠٦ طبعت عام ١٢٩٢ بولاق القاهرة.
أحمد الصعيدي العدوي المتوفي سنة ١١٨٩ يوجد في الجزائر والقاهرة.

Ahmad al-Sa'idi al-Adawi, who died in the year 1189 AH; it exists in Algeria and Cairo.
(1) 'Uqud al-Jawahir, logic books; al-'Uqud al-Lu'lu'iyya, logic books.

Commentary
This passage lists the glossators (hawashi) who composed marginal notes on al-Sullam. It names Muhammad ibn Ali al-Sabban (d. 1206 AH), whose gloss was printed in Bulaq, Cairo, in 1292 AH. It then names Ahmad al-Sa'idi al-Adawi (d. 1189 AH), whose gloss is found in Algeria and Cairo. The footnote cites the standard Algerian bibliographic sources for these works. Together with the preceding list of commentators, this passage shows that the Sullam generated both extensive commentaries and shorter glosses, reflecting its central place in the logic curriculum of the Islamic West.

How Sharh al-Sullam Became a Canonical Text
Passage assesses the book's fame, curricular role, and scholarly influence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the factors that led to Sharh al-Sullam becoming a widely circulated curriculum text in Islamic logic.

Core Idea
A text's value is measured by how scholars engage with it—through circulation, commentary, and correction.

This passage provides a rare assessment from within the tradition of how al-Akhdari's commentary achieved its canonical status. It reveals that a work becomes a classical text not merely by being written, but by being adopted, examined, and refined by generations of scholars. Understanding this process helps you appreciate how Islamic logical works were transmitted and validated in the madrasa system.

Guided Path
1
Identify the text's praised qualities
Read the opening phrases: 'precious source, abundant in material, captivating in expression'. These indicate a subjective scholarly appraisal that contributed to the text's popularity.
2
Trace the circulation evidence
The phrase 'tadāwalahā kathīr...' (many circulated it) shows the work was actively transmitted. Note the agents: scholars who looked at the commentators of Sullam.
3
Distinguish 'al-madkhal' from 'muqarraran'
'Al-madkhal' means it served as an introduction to the field; 'muqarraran' means it was officially set in the curriculum. Both are distinct stages of canonization.
4
Observe the two modes of reception: sharḥ and istidrāk
Commentary (sharḥ) expands and explains; corrective addenda (istidrāk) critique and refine. Both indicate deep engagement.
5
Reflect on the institutional adoption
The text became famous in the Islamic world and was prescribed at al-Azhar. This shows how a madrasa curriculum can elevate a work to canonical status.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
العلماء
فرسالة شرح متن السلم المرونق في علم المنطق تعتبر مصدراً نفيساً في بابها غزيرة في مادتها أخاذة في عبارتها فقد تداولها كثير من انظر شراح السلم واعتنوا بها في هذا الفن وألفوا فيه وتعتبر المدخل في بابها وتنسيقها وهي أول متن في علم المنطق وصل إلى التداول بين أيدي العلماء بعد زمن المؤلف واشتهر في العالم الإسلامي وأصبح مقرراً على المعاهد الكبرى كالأزهر الشريف وتأثر به العلماء شرحاً واستدراكاً
The Scholars
So the epistle Sharh Matn al-Sullam al-Murawnaq in the science of logic is considered a precious source in its field, abundant in its material, captivating in its expression; for many of [those who] look [at] the commentators of Sullam have circulated it, and they cared for it in this art and authored in it, and it is considered the introduction in its field and its organization, and it is the first matn in the science of logic that reached circulation among the hands of the scholars after the time of the author, and it became famous in the Islamic world and became a set text upon the great institutes such as the Noble Azhar, and the scholars were influenced by it through commentary and correction.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage evaluates the external scholarly status of al-Akhdari's commentary. It appears to open with the heading 'al-Ulama' (The Scholars), then proceeds to describe Sharh Matn al-Sullam al-Murawnaq as a precious source in its field, abundant in material, and captivating in expression. The author notes that many of those engaged with the commentaries on Sullam circulated this work, cared for it, and authored further works in the discipline because of it. The text identifies it as the introductory work (al-madkhal) in its subject and arrangement, and as the first matn in logic to be circulated among scholars after the author's era. Its fame spread throughout the Islamic world until it became a set text (muqarrar) at great institutes such as the Noble Azhar. Finally, the passage observes that later scholars were influenced by it through both commentary (sharh) and corrective addenda (istidrak), indicating its foundational role in the post-Akhdari tradition.

The Commentary's Method and Scholarly Engagement
Praises the commentary's clarity and engagement with authorities

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the intellectual interlocutors of the Sulam commentary and explain the significance of engaging with al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib.

Core Idea
The Sulam commentary is not a beginner's summary—it enters into critical dialogue with the giants of logic.

This passage from the commentary's introduction reveals the author's approach: he clarifies obscurities (mubhamat) and engages directly with the greatest authorities (jahbadhat). Understanding this helps you appreciate the commentary's depth and situate it within the broader logical tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key terms
Look for the two technical terms: 'mubhamat' (obscure points) and 'jahbadhat' (great scholars). They indicate the commentary's dual focus: clarifying difficult material and engaging with authoritative figures.
2
Analyze how the commentary treats mubhamat
The passage says the commentary 'uncovered the veil' on obscure points and 'contained them from its lengthy discussions,' meaning it isolates and explains difficult concepts without unnecessary digression.
This shows the commentary's pedagogical efficiency.
3
Note the shift to the logical side
The text then turns to 'al-nahiyya al-mantiqiyya' (the logical perspective), where the commentary engages with specific towering scholars.
This shift indicates a move from general praise to specific scholarly engagement.
4
Identify the named scholars
The passage explicitly names Fakhr al-Din al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib as the 'jahbadhat al-ulama' (great scholars) with whom the commentary enters into conversation.
These two are central figures in logic and usul al-fiqh, respectively.
5
Reflect on the significance
Why mention these two? Because al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib shaped the post-Avicennan logical tradition. Engaging them signals that the commentary is a serious scholarly work, not a mere summary.
This helps you understand the commentary's intellectual ambition.

وقد كشف القناع في هذا الشرح عن مبهمات علم المنطق واحتواها من مطولاته حيث يفسر المصطلحات تفسير نفيساً بسيطاً وعميقاً فإذا ذهبنا إلى الناحية المنطقية فإنه يتكلم عن جهابذة العلماء كالفخر الرازي وابن الحاجب

This passage discusses the internal methodological merits of the commentary. It states that al-Akhdari uncovered the obscure points (mubhamat) of logic and addressed them apart from lengthy discussions, explaining technical terms with an explanation that is precious, simple, and profound. The text then shifts to the logical perspective specifically, noting that the commentary engages with the great authorities of the discipline, naming Fakhr al-Din al-Razi and Ibn al-Hajib as the towering scholars with whom al-Akhdari enters into critical conversation. This shows that the work is not merely a pedagogical summary but a serious engagement with the logical tradition.

Sources and Intellectual Foundations of al-Akhdarī's Commentary
Introductory survey of al-Akhdarī's sources and commentary scope.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main sources and intellectual disciplines that underpin al-Akhdarī's Sharḥ al-Sullam and assess its authority claims.

Core Idea
A commentary's authority rests on its sources, not just on its claims.

This passage introduces the intellectual genealogy of al-Akhdarī's Sharḥ al-Sullam, listing the key works and sciences that shaped it. Understanding this genealogy helps you evaluate the commentary's authority and situate it within the broader Islamic tradition. The following guided path will walk you through analyzing the sources and the author's appraisal of his own work.

Guided Path
1
List the named sources and their authors
Identify the five specific works mentioned in the passage and their respective authors. This forms the core of al-Akhdarī's cited sources.
Use the Arabic names as given; cross-check with your knowledge of the authors if possible.
2
Identify the intellectual disciplines mentioned
Note the sciences listed: logic, grammar, language, uṣūl al-fiqh, philosophy, and kalām. Recognise that the commentary draws on multiple fields, not just logic.
Disciplines like grammar and uṣūl al-fiqh indicate a broader methodological scope.
3
Analyze the author's appraisal of the commentary
Read the passage's description of the Sharḥ: it is 'precious', 'abundant', 'captivating', lifts veils from obscurities, explains terms simply yet profoundly. Determine what claims of authority and quality are being made.
The appraisal serves to establish the commentary's stature as a reference work.
4
Evaluate the claim of comprehensiveness
The passage mentions that the commentary engages both logical (Ashʿarī, Muʿtazilī, Qadarī) and grammatical (Basran, Kufan) schools. Assess whether this claim is supported by the listing of sources and scholars.
Comprehensiveness is a key argument for the commentary's authority.
5
Reflect on the institutional reception
The passage states that the commentary became a set text at al-Azhar and other institutes. Consider how this external validation reinforces the internal claims of quality.
Institutional adoption is a real-world measure of a work's influence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المصادر التي اعتمد عليها الأخضري في شرح سلمه
هذه رسالة حصيلة عدة كتب في علم المنطق والنحو واللغة وأصول الفقه والفلسفة والمنطق والكلام منها :
- المطالب لفخر الدين الرازي.
- المستصفى للإمام الغزالي.
- المطالع لقطب الدين الشيرازي.
- الأمل والصول في علمي الأصول والجدل لابن الحاجب.
- البرهان للإمام الجويني.
العلماء
فرسالة شرح متن السلم المرونق في علم المنطق تعتبر مصدراً نفيساً في بابها غزيرة في مادتها أخاذة في عبارتها فقد تداولها كثير من [؟] شراح السلم واعتنوا بها في هذا الفن وألفوا فيه وتعتبر المدخل في بابها وتنسيقها وهي أول متن في علم المنطق وصل إلى التداول بين أيدي العلماء بعد زمن المؤلف واشتهر في العالم الإسلامي وأصبح مقرراً على المعاهد الكبرى كالأزهر الشريف وتأثر به العلماء شرحاً واستدراكاً وقد كشف القناع في هذا الشرح عن مبهمات علم المنطق واحتواها من مطولاته حيث يفسر المصطلحات تفسيراً نفيساً بسيطاً وعميقاً فإذا ذهبنا إلى الناحية المنطقية فإنه يتكلم عن جهابذة العلماء كالفخر الرازي وابن الحاجب والغزالي والباقلاني والقطب الشيرازي وكذا المذاهب والفرق كالأشاعرة والمعتزلة والقدرية، وإذا ذهبنا إلى الناحية اللغوية والنحوية فإنه يذكر الخلاف في المذاهب النحوية كالمدرسة البصرية والمدرسة الكوفية وال[؟] ويعتمد على فطاحلة هذا الفن كسيبويه والكسائي وأبي زيد الأنصاري وابن المبرد والنحاس وغيرهم فنجده مستشهداً بكلام وشعر العرب ومحققاً ومترجماً ومناقشاً لرجال هذا الفن وغيره من العلوم فجاءت رسالته هذه رسالة عظيمة في بابها مفيدة في معناها، فجاء شرحه هذا مصدراً ومرجعاً يرجع إليه في علم المنطق.
The sources which al-Akhḍarī relied upon in his Sharḥ Sullam
This treatise is the product of numerous books in the science of logic, grammar, language, the principles of jurisprudence, philosophy, logic, and theology. Among them are:
- al-Matālib of Fakhr al-Dīn al-Rāzī.
- al-Mustaṣfā of Imām al-Ghazālī.
- al-Matāliʿ of Quṭb al-Dīn al-Shīrāzī.
- al-Amal wa al-Ṣūl fī ʿIlmay al-Uṣūl wa al-Jadal of Ibn al-Ḥājib.
- al-Burhān of Imām al-Juwaynī.
The scholars
As for the treatise Sharḥ Matn al-Sullam al-Murawnaq fī ʿIlm al-Manṭiq, it is considered a precious source in its field, abundant in its material, captivating in its expression. Many [؟] of the commentators of al-Sullam have circulated it, cared for it in this art, and composed works in it. It is considered the introduction to its field and its arrangement. It is the first text in the science of logic that reached circulation among the hands of scholars after the time of its author, and it became famous in the Islamic world and became a set text in the great institutes such as al-Azhar al-Sharīf. Scholars were influenced by it through commentary and supplementation. In this Sharḥ, the veil has been lifted from the obscurities of the science of logic and he encompassed them from its lengthy works, whereby he explains the technical terms with a precious, simple, and profound explanation. If we turn to the logical aspect, he speaks about the giants of the scholars such as Fakhr al-Rāzī and Ibn al-Ḥājib, al-Ghazālī and al-Bāqillānī and Quṭb al-Shīrāzī, as well as the schools and sects such as the Ashʿarīs, the Muʿtazilites, and the Qadarites. If we turn to the linguistic and grammatical aspect, he mentions the disagreement in the grammatical schools such as the Basran school, the Kufan school, and the [؟], and he relies on the luminaries of this art such as Sībawayh, al-Kisāʾī, Abū Zayd al-Anṣārī, Ibn al-Mubarrad, al-Naḥḥās, and others. Thus we find him citing the speech and poetry of the Arabs, verifying, glossing, and discussing the men of this art and other sciences. So this treatise of his came as a mighty treatise in its field, beneficial in its meaning. Thus this Sharḥ of his came as a source and a reference to which one returns in the science of logic.
Source pages p. 15

Commentary
This passage is introductory front matter that catalogues the intellectual foundations of al-Akhḍarī’s commentary and then asserts its scholarly authority. The author begins by stating that the commentary is a harvest of many books across manifold Islamic sciences: logic, Arabic grammar, language, uṣūl al-fiqh, philosophy, and kalām. He then names five specific sources—works by Fakhr al-Dīn al-Rāzī, al-Ghazālī, Quṭb al-Dīn al-Shīrāzī, Ibn al-Ḥājib, and Imām al-Juwaynī—thereby anchoring the commentary in the central tradition of Islamic intellectual production rather than in isolated speculation. After this bibliographic foundation, the passage turns to appraising the commentary itself. It describes Sharḥ Matn al-Sullam al-Murawnaq as a precious source, rich in content and elegant in expression, noting that later scholars circulated it, wrote further works around it, and elevated it to the status of a prescribed text at major institutes such as al-Azhar. The passage emphasizes that the commentary lifts the veil from the obscurities of logic and extracts what is needed from otherwise lengthy works, presenting technical terminology in a manner that is at once precious, simple, and profound. The author then expands the scope beyond pure logic: on the logical side, al-Akhḍarī engages the great authorities such as al-Rāzī, Ibn al-Ḥājib, al-Ghazālī, al-Bāqillānī, and al-Shīrāzī, as well as the sects—the Ashʿarīs, Muʿtazilites, and Qadarites; on the linguistic side, he traverses the grammatical schools of Basra and Kufa and relies on the foundational grammarians such as Sībawayh and al-Kisāʾī. The passage concludes by praising the work as a mighty, beneficial treatise and a permanent reference in the science of logic.

Key Terms
المنطق (al-manṭiq): The science of logic; identified here as both the subject of the commentary and one of the fields from which al-Akhḍarī drew his sources.
الجدل (al-jadal): Dialectic or disputation; mentioned here as the field of Ibn al-Ḥājib’s source work and as part of the methodological background of the commentary. [Note: In early uṣūl works jadal refers to structured disputation; in later mantiq it is sometimes distinguished from burhān as a lesser form of proof.]
أصول الفقه (uṣūl al-fiqh): The principles of Islamic jurisprudence; listed among the sciences underpinning the commentary’s material.
الشرح (al-sharḥ): The commentary itself (this work), praised as a reference that unveils obscurities and explains technical terms in a simple yet profound manner. [Note: In this context al-sharḥ is a running exposition of the matn; in other contexts it can refer more broadly to any explanatory work.]
المصطلحات (al-muṣṭalaḥāt): The technical terminologies of logic; the author explains them in a manner described as precious, simple, and profound.

Key Takeaway
Al-Akhḍarī's Sharḥ draws its authority from a broad interdisciplinary foundation, integrating logic, grammar, uṣūl al-fiqh, and kalām, as evidenced by the diverse sources it cites.

Interdisciplinary Foundations of the Logic Commentary
Editor describes the author's comprehensive interdisciplinary methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major theological and linguistic disciplines and authorities that the author integrates in his commentary on logic.

Core Idea
Logic in the Islamic tradition is nourished by kalam and nahw, not isolated from them.

This passage from the editor's introduction reveals the comprehensive methodology of the commentator. He draws not only on the science of logic itself, but on the great theologians and grammatical schools of the Islamic intellectual heritage. Understanding this interdisciplinary approach is essential for grasping how the commentary serves as a reference (marji') for the student of logic — it is not a narrow treatise, but a work that situates logical reasoning within the broader landscape of Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the theological authorities and schools mentioned
Scan the Arabic for names of theologians and schools: al-Ghazali, al-Baqillani, al-Qutb al-Shirazi, Ash'ariyya, Mu'tazila, Qadariyya. These represent the kalam tradition that the author engages with.
2
Identify the linguistic/grammatical dimension
Look for 'الناحية اللغوية والنحوية' and the schools named: Basran, Kufan, and the unclear 'al-Shalubayn'. Also note the names of leading grammarians: Sibawayh, al-Kisa'i, etc.
3
Observe the author's method of engagement
The editor says the author cites Arab speech and poetry, verifies (muhaqqiq), comments (mutarjim), and discusses scholars. This shows a critical, scholarly approach, not mere citation.
4
Recognize the passage's purpose
The editor concludes that the treatise is 'tremendous in its scope, beneficial in its meaning', and presents the commentary as a source and reference for the science of logic. This frames the work's authority.

How to Evaluate Manuscript Witnesses in Islamic Textual Scholarship
Editor lists the two manuscripts relied upon for this edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to assess the reliability of a manuscript witness based on its script, date, marginal annotations, and provenance.

Core Idea
A critical edition rests on careful comparison of manuscript witnesses.

In this lesson, you will examine how an editor describes two manuscripts used to establish the text of al-Akhdari's logical work. Pay attention to the details that matter for textual criticism, such as script, dating, marginal notes, and physical dimensions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two manuscripts (A and B)
Find the designations and locations: manuscript A is from the National Library (number 2379), manuscript B is the editor's personal copy. Note their sigla (أ) and (ب).
Sigla are short codes used to refer to each witness.
2
Examine the script and dating
Manuscript A is written in Maghribi script, described as 'excellent on the whole'. It was copied in 1198 AH, about two centuries after the original composition.
Script and dating help assess likelihood of textual corruption.
3
Note marginal features
Manuscript A contains 'takhrijat' (marginal annotations). These may indicate corrections, variant readings, or scholarly commentary.
Marginal notes can be important for reconstructing the text's transmission.
4
Assess completeness and physical description
Manuscript A has 17 pages, 35 lines per page, dimensions 25 x 10. This helps estimate how much text it contains and whether it is likely a complete copy.
Physical description aids in identifying the manuscript type (e.g., a student copy vs. a master copy).
5
Evaluate the editor's choice to rely on both
The editor uses two independent witnesses. This increases confidence in the text: variant readings in one can be checked against the other.
Having multiple witnesses is a cornerstone of critical edition methodology.

This passage is editorial front matter in which the editor lists the manuscript witnesses used to establish the text. The editor states that his prior research efforts produced two manuscripts of al-Akhdari's Sharh Matn al-Sullam al-Murawnaq. The manuscript comprises 17 pages with 35 lines per page, with dimensions of 25 by 10. The second manuscript, designated (B), is the editor's personal copy held in his library. A footnote adds that the index was reproduced by computer.

Manuscript Witnesses and Sigla in Editing Islamic Logic Texts
Editor describes two manuscript sources relied upon for the edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and compare manuscript witnesses using physical descriptions and sigla.

Core Idea
Every printed edition depends on manuscript choices — the sigla tell the story.

This passage is typical of editorial front matter in critical editions. The editor assigns each manuscript a siglum (letter) and describes its physical features, date, and provenance. Understanding this process helps you evaluate the reliability of any printed text of a classical logic work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two sigla
Find the letters (أ) and (ب) in the Arabic and note which manuscript each refers to. The first (أ) is the National Library copy, the second (ب) is the editor's personal copy.
Sigla are abbreviations used to refer to manuscripts throughout the edition.
2
Compare the physical descriptions
Look at the script, dimensions, number of lines, and presence of marginal notes. The first manuscript has Maghribi script, 35 lines per page, and marginal takhrījāt. The second has Algerian script, is written in black and red ink, but lacks details like line count.
Physical details help identify the manuscript and assess its production quality.
3
Note date and copyist information
The first manuscript is dated 1198 AH and has a named copyist, Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Shawli. The second has no date or copyist name. This affects the weight given to each witness.
A dated, named copy allows us to trace provenance and estimate textual transmission delay.
4
Assess reliability
Consider age, provenance, and completeness. The first is older but still about two centuries after the original; the second is of unknown date. The editor likely uses both to cross-check readings.
No single manuscript is perfect; multiple witnesses strengthen the edition.

Commentary
This passage is editorial front matter in which the modern editor of the commentary on al-Akhdari’s Sullam al-Murawnaq describes the two manuscript witnesses he relied upon to establish his edition. He begins by stating that his prior research produced two manuscript copies of the Sharh. He records its shelf number, the fact that it is bound with another commentary on the Sullam by Ibrahim Sa‘id Qadura al-Jaza’iri, its Maghribi script, the presence of marginal takhrījāt, its copyist’s name and nisba, its date of 1198 AH, and its physical dimensions. The passage is doing the work of classical textual criticism: establishing the documentary basis for the edition so that readers can assess the reliability of the transmitted text.

Takhrījāt: Tracking Citations in Manuscript Margins
Editor describes two manuscript sources relied upon for the edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the function of takhrījāt in manuscript margins and recognise their role in scholarly transmission.

Core Idea
Marginal takhrījāt are not decoration — they are the scholar's proof that every quoted line has a source.

In the first manuscript description, the editor notes that the margins contain 'تخريجات' (takhrījāt). In hadith science, takhrij means tracing a hadith to its original sources. But here, in a logic commentary, it means the copyist or a later reader added marginal notes identifying the sources of quotations — for example, where al-Akhdari or the commentator got their examples. This practice shows how seriously scholars took the accuracy of citations.

Guided Path
1
Find the word in the Arabic passage
Locate the word 'تخريجات' in the description of the first manuscript. It appears after the mention of the script and before the date.
The word is in the plural form; singular is takhrīja.
2
Understand the shift in meaning
In hadith studies, takhrij is a technical method of tracing a hadith through its chain of transmission. Here, it refers to marginal notes that likely identify the sources of quotations, such as Quranic verses or earlier scholarly works.
The core idea is the same: source identification.
3
Analyse the purpose
Why would a copyist or owner add such notes? To help future readers verify the accuracy of quotations. In a logic commentary, an incorrect attribution could lead to a flawed understanding of an argument.
This reflects the Islamic tradition's emphasis on 'isnad' (chain of transmission) even for written scholarship.
4
Connect to the logic text
Al-Akhdari's Sullam uses examples from various Islamic sciences. A takhrīja might note that a particular syllogism example comes from al-Ghazali's works, allowing the reader to check the original context.
Source verification ensures that the logical principles are correctly attributed.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

My efforts in research previously yielded copies of the book Sharh Matn al-Sullam al-Murawnaq fi ‘Ilm al-Mantiq by al-Akhdari, in obtaining two manuscript copies: the first is the copy of the National Library and I symbolized it with the letter (A), and the second is my copy which is present in our library and I symbolized it with the letter (B), and this is the description of the two relied-upon copies: the first, the copy of the National Library, falls under number: 2379 and with it is Sharh al-Sullam by Ibrahim Sa‘id Qadura al-Jaza’iri — the script is Maghribi, generally commendable, and on the margins of the pages are takhrījāt. — Date of copying: copied in the year 1198 AH. Its copyist: Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Musa al-Shawli al-Sadmi watan, and we note that its date of copying is distant from the original copy by approximately two centuries. Number of folios: 17, each page having 35 lines. — Length: 25. — Width: 10. The second: it is from the stock of my library and I have enumerated it in our catalog named ‘Majmu‘at Balqasim Dayf li-l-Makhtutat al-Qism al-Awwal (1),’ and it falls under number: 153 — Logic section... — The script is beautiful Algerian, tending toward clarity, written inside a book frame with black and red ink. — Length: 17. — Width: 11. Date of copying: it is devoid of the copyist’s name and date of its copying.
Source pages p. 17

Commentary
This passage is editorial front matter in which the modern editor of the commentary on al-Akhdari’s Sullam al-Murawnaq describes the two manuscript witnesses he relied upon to establish his edition. He begins by stating that his prior research produced two manuscript copies of the Sharh. He then identifies the first witness by its institutional home — the National Library — and assigns it the siglum (أ). He records its shelf number, the fact that it is bound with another commentary on the Sullam by Ibrahim Sa‘id Qadura al-Jaza’iri, its Maghribi script, the presence of marginal takhrījāt, its copyist’s name and nisba, its date of 1198 AH, and its physical dimensions. He notes that this copy is separated from the original by roughly two centuries. He then turns to the second witness, his own private copy, assigning it the siglum (ب). He records its catalog number within his personal collection, describes its Algerian script and use of red and black ink, gives its dimensions, and notes that it lacks both a copyist’s name and a date. The passage is doing the work of classical textual criticism: establishing the documentary basis for the edition so that readers can assess the reliability of the transmitted text.

Evaluating a Critical Edition of a Logic Text
Editor explains manuscript sources and editorial methodology for a logic text edition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the reliability of a printed edition of a classical Islamic logic text by analyzing its manuscript basis, editorial methodology, and reference works used.

Core Idea
A scholarly edition is only as reliable as its manuscript collation and lexical apparatus.

This passage is not logic itself but the scholarly apparatus that makes the study of logic possible. The modern editor describes how he prepared a critical edition of al-Akhdari's Sharh al-Sullam al-Murawnaq. By examining his manuscript sources, choice of base text, and the reference works he used, we can learn to assess the trustworthiness of any printed edition of a classical work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the manuscripts used by the editor
The editor mentions two manuscripts: one from a library (numbered 153), and one from his personal collection. Note the description: Algerian script, undated, black and red ink. This tells you whether the manuscript is likely early or late, and its provenance.
The absence of a copyist name and date reduces certainty about the manuscript's age.
2
Examine the choice of base printed edition
The editor selected the Bulaq edition because it included al-Damanhuri's hashiya. This choice is justified by the need for auxiliary glosses that help produce a sound text. Recognize that a base text with marginal glosses can offer more clarity than a bare text.
The fact that the Bulaq edition was published multiple times indicates its popularity, but not necessarily its accuracy.
3
Assess the reference works used for textual criticism
The editor relied on two dictionaries of technical terms: al-Manawi's al-Tawqif and al-Jurjani's al-Ta'rifat. These are standard lexical works in the Islamic sciences. Their use shows the editor's commitment to precise terminology.
Familiarity with such dictionaries is crucial for any scholar working with classical texts.
4
Check the scope of the editor's commentary and glossary
The editor says he commented on all logical issues and produced a glossary of terms. This means the edition is more than a raw text: it includes explanatory notes that aid understanding.
A critical edition with commentary and glossary is usually more helpful for students than a bare text.

The second [manuscript]: it is from the stock of my library and I have enumerated it in our catalogue named 'The Collection of Belqasem Daif of Manuscripts, Part One' (1), and it falls under number: 153 — Logic Section... — The script is beautiful Algerian, tending toward clarity, written inside a frame with black and red ink. — Length: 17. — Width: 11. Date of copying: it is devoid of the copyist's name and has no date of copying. My methodology in preparation and verification (1): My work encompassed the Sharh al-Sullam al-Murawnaq fi 'Ilm al-Mantiq by al-Akhdari, and the commentary has been published before several times, once independently, and another time accompanied by glosses. I chose from the old editions the Bulaq edition, and in its margin the commentary of al-Damanhuri entitled (Idah al-Mubham min Ma'ani al-Sullam), and I found in it what helps me to produce a sound and precise text. Therefore I carefully collated between the printed copies and the two manuscripts, and I relied on a number of linguistic and logical dictionaries, such as al-Tawqif 'ala Muhimmat al-Ta'arif by al-Manawi and al-Ta'rifat by al-Sharif al-Jurjani, from which I benefited greatly in producing the text and knowing the logical terminology. Nor should I fail to mention the commentary of the scholar 'Abd al-Rahim Faraj al-Jundi, formerly inspector at the Azhari institutes and currently teacher at the Islamic Studies of the Higher Division at al-Azhar, in his valuable book 'Sharh al-Sullam'. And likewise Mugniyat al-Tullab Sharh Matn Isaghuji by the scholar Athir al-Din al-Abhari, edited by Mahmud Ramadan al-Bouti. And I commented on all the logical issues that the Shaykh al-Akhdari addressed in his commentary on his Sullam, and I also produced [a glossary of] the terminology.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is editorial front matter in which the modern editor describes his manuscript sources and his methodology for preparing the printed edition of al-Akhdari's Sharh al-Sullam al-Murawnaq. He begins by cataloguing a second manuscript from his personal library — an Algerian manuscript of unknown date, numbered 153 in the logic section, notable for its clear script in black and red ink. He then turns to his editorial method. He explains that since al-Akhdari's commentary on the Sullam had been printed multiple times, both alone and with glosses, he selected the Bulaq edition as his base text because it included al-Damanhuri's hashiya, Idah al-Mubham, which he found helpful for establishing a sound text. He then describes the philological and logical reference works he consulted to resolve terminology: al-Manawi's al-Tawqif 'ala Muhimmat al-Ta'arif and al-Jurjani's al-Ta'rifat, both standard reference works for technical terms in the Islamic sciences. He also acknowledges the modern commentary of al-Jundi and the edited version of al-Abhari's Isaghuji by al-Bouti. Finally, he notes that he has provided commentary on all the logical topics treated by al-Akhdari and has produced a glossary of technical terms. This passage is not logic per se but rather the scholarly apparatus that makes the study of the text possible; it shows how the editor navigated between manuscript evidence, printed tradition, and lexicographical tools to produce a reliable edition.

Understanding the Editor's Methodology for Textual Verification
Editor describes his method, sources, and tools for verifying the text.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the key steps a critical editor takes to produce a reliable text edition, as demonstrated by the editor of al-Akhdari's Sharh al-Sullam.

Core Idea
A reliable text edition requires comparing manuscripts, consulting dictionaries, and acknowledging earlier commentaries.

This passage is not a logical lesson itself, but it teaches us how to approach any classical text: with careful methodology. The editor of al-Akhdari's Sharh al-Sullam explains his process of selecting the base edition, comparing manuscripts, using dictionaries for terminology, and incorporating earlier commentaries. Understanding this methodology is essential for anyone who wants to use critical editions in Islamic scholarship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text chosen
Look at what edition he selected and why. He chose the Bulaq print because it includes al-Damanhuri's gloss, which helps produce a sound and accurate text.
The base text is the starting point for collation.
2
Note the sources used for comparison
He compared the Bulaq print with two manuscripts. This collation (muqabala) is crucial for identifying variants and correcting errors.
Multiple witnesses increase reliability.
3
Recognize the dictionaries consulted
He used al-Tawqif 'ala Muhimmat al-Ta'arif by al-Manawi and al-Ta'rifat by al-Jurjani. These specialized dictionaries clarify logical terminology.
Dictionaries ensure precise understanding of technical terms.
4
Identify the later commentaries acknowledged
He mentions al-Jundi's Sharh al-Sullam and al-Abhari's Mughni al-Tullab. These works represent the commentarial tradition he builds upon.
Acknowledging previous scholarship shows scholarly continuity.
5
Observe the final outputs
He comments on all logical topics, extracts terminology, collects verses and hadiths, and compiles a glossary. This is the product of his methodology.
The final edition includes multiple layers of utility.
